25:Td04e,<entryFree id="n25689" key="ضَرَبَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">ضَرَبَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">ضَرِبَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, O, K, &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">ضَرْبٌ</foreign>, (S, O, &amp;c.,) [<hi rend="ital">He beat, struck, smote,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">hit, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi>] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25689-1" target="ضرّبهُ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n25689"/></foreign> [signifies the same in an intensive sense, i. e. <hi rend="ital">he beat,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, much,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">violently;</hi> or in a frequentative sense, i. e. <hi rend="ital">several,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">many, times:</hi> or rather <foreign lang="ar">ضرّب</foreign> is used in relation to several, or many, objects, as will be shown in what follows]: (K:) accord. to Er-Rághib, <foreign lang="ar">الضَّرْبُ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">the making a thing to fall upon another thing;</hi> and, as some say, <hi rend="ital">the making it to fall with violence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vehemence.</hi> (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَهُ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He struck him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, with it</hi>], i. e. with a sword, (A, Mgh, Msb), &amp;c. (A, Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">تَضْرِبُ فِى حَدِيدٍ بَارِدٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Thou beatest upon cold iron</hi>]: a prov. [expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">حد</foreign>]. (Har p. 633.) And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُ زَيْدًا سَوْطًا</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِسَوْطٍ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">I struck Zeyd with a whip</hi>], or <foreign lang="ar">ضَرْبَةَ سَوْطٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">a stroke of a whip</hi>]: (M in art. <foreign lang="ar">سوط</foreign>, q. v.:) and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَهُ مِائَةَ سَوْطٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He struck him a hundred strokes of the whip</hi>]. (S and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">سحل</foreign>, &amp;c.) And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُ عُنُقَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I smote his neck,</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">I beheaded him</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n25689-2" target="ضَرَّبْتُ" n="2" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>الأَعْنَاقَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I smote the necks,</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">I struck off the heads</hi>]; the teshdeed denoting muchness [of the <pb n="1778"/> action] or multiplicity [of the objects]: AZ says that, when the object is one, the Arabs use only the former verb, without teshdeed; but when there is a plurality of objects, either of the verbs; (Msb;) [so that] one says, <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبُوا أَعْنَاقَهُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They smote their necks,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beheaded them</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">أَمَرَ  <ref cref="n25689-3" target="بِتَضْرِيبِ" n="3" type="6" subtype="FTFSO" lang="ar"/> الرِّقَابِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He gave the order to smite the necks,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">to strike off the heads</hi>]: (A:) <foreign lang="ar">فَضَرْبَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الرِّقَابِ</foreign> in the Kur xlvii. 4 is originally <foreign lang="ar">فَٱضْرِبُوا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الرِّقَابَ ضَرْبًا</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">Then do ye smite the necks,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">strike off the heads</hi>]; (Bd;) the inf. n. being here put for its verb. (Jel.) [Respecting the phrase <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ ٱلْيَضْرِبُكَ</foreign>, see 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">جدع</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [Hence a variety of meanings and phrases here following.]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ كَلْبَهُ عَلَى الصَّيْدِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He beat,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">disciplined,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">trained, his dog for the purpose of the chase</hi>]: whence the phrases <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ عَلَيْهِ جِرْوَتَهُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ جِرْوَةَ نَفْسِهِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُ جِرْوَتِى عَنْهُ</foreign> [expl. voce <foreign lang="ar">جِرْوَةٌ</foreign>]. (Z, and TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">جرو</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">لَا تُضْرَبُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَكْبَادُ الإِبِلِ إِلَّا ثَلَاثَةِ مَسَاجِدَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Camels shall not be ridden, save to three mosques:</hi> [namely, that of Mekkeh, that of El-Medeeneh, and that of El-Aksà at Jerusalem:] a trad. (TA. [See also 4 in art. <foreign lang="ar">عمل</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ بِهِ الأَرْضَ</foreign>, lit. <hi rend="ital">He smote with him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, the ground;</hi> meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">he cast, threw,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">flung, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, upon the ground.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ بِسَلْحِهِ الأَرْضَ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He cast forth his excrement,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ordure, upon the ground.</hi>] And [hence] <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الأَرْضَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">الغَائِطَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He voided excrement,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ordure;</hi> (A, TA;) and so <foreign lang="ar">الخَلَآءَ</foreign>. (TA.) [<foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ بِنَفْسِهِ الأَرْضَ</foreign> see expl. in the latter half of this paragraph.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبْتُ القَوْسَ بِالمِضْرَبِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I struck the string of the bow with the wooden implement</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">mallet</hi>] <hi rend="ital">used in separating cotton.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ العُودَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He struck the chords of the lute;</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">he played upon the lute;</hi> and so <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ بِالعُودِ</foreign>]. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الوَتِدَ</foreign>, aor. and inf. n. as above, <hi rend="ital">He beat</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">knocked</hi> or <hi rend="ital">struck</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the tent-peg,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stake, so that it became firm in the ground.</hi> (Lh, TA.) And [hence] <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الخَيْمَةَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He pitched the tent, by knocking in its pegs with a mallet:</hi> (Kull p. 231:) or <hi rend="ital">he set up the tent.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الدِّرْهَمَ</foreign>, aor. and inf. n. as above, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He struck, coined,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">minted, the dirhem,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">piece of money.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ عَلَى ٱسمِهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He struck, coined,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">minted,</hi> money <hi rend="ital">in his name</hi>]. (ISd, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">جوز</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَكْتُوبِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He sealed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stamped, the writing.</hi> (A, * TA.) [And <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He erased it;</hi> namely, anything written.]          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الطِّينَ عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الجِدَارِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He stuck,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">applied, the mud upon the wall,</hi> as a plaster]. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="35">-b35-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ مَثَلًا</foreign> (S, A, O, &amp;c.) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He rehearsed, propounded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">declared, a parable, a similitude, an example,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a proverb;</hi> said of God [and of a man]: (S, * O, * Msb, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">he mentioned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">set forth, a parable,</hi> &amp;c.: or <hi rend="ital">he framed a parable:</hi> thus expl., the verb has but one objective complement: or the phrase signifies <hi rend="ital">he made</hi> [such a thing] <hi rend="ital">an example,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the subject of a parable</hi> or <hi rend="ital">similitude</hi> &amp;c.; and so has two objective complements: in the saying in the Kur [xxxvi. 12] <foreign lang="ar">وَٱضْرِبْ لَهُمْ مَثَلًا أَصْحَابَ ٱلْقَرْيَةِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">And propound thou to them a parable, the people of the town</hi>] i. e., the story of the people of the town, [or <hi rend="ital">make thou to them a parable,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">similitude,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an example, the people of the town;</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">مثلا</foreign> may be in the accus. case as an objective complement, <foreign lang="ar">اضحاب القرية</foreign> being a substitute for <foreign lang="ar">مثلا</foreign>; or <foreign lang="ar">اصحاب القرية</foreign> may be regarded as a second objective complement [i. e. second in the order of the words, but first in the order of the sense]: the phrase is differently expl. on account of the different meanings of the verb <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ</foreign>; which signifies <hi rend="ital">he described,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rehearsed;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he declared, propounded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">explained;</hi> and <hi rend="ital">he made, caused to be,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">constituted;</hi> &amp;c.; accord. to some, it is taken from the phrase <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الدِرْهَمَ</foreign> [q. v.]; because of the impression which a parable or the like makes upon the mind: accord. to some, from <foreign lang="ar">ضَرِيبٌ</foreign> signifying “ a like; ” because the first thing is made like the second: accord. to some, from <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ الطِّينَ عَلَى الجِدَارِ</foreign> [q. v.; because the mud, applied as a plaster, conforms to the shape of the wall]: and accord. to some, from <foreign lang="ar">ضَرَبَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الخَاتَمَ</foreign> [q. v.]; because of the correspondence between a parable or the like and the object to which it is applied, and the correspondence between the signet and its impression.
